{"parentUuid":"a2af6760-4119-4928-aaa5-2170d159daa4","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"67fcde4a-7483-4526-a2da-9ae9514890c8","agentId":"a5cf7829dab911586","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_014qoiEPbtegiBGw1Her7sfT","type":"tool_result","content":"# Symphony Service Specification\n\nStatus: Draft v1 (language-agnostic)\n\nPurpose: Define a service that orchestrates coding agents to get project work done.\n\n## 1. Problem Statement\n\nSymphony is a long-running automation service that continuously reads work from an issue tracker\n(Linear in this specification version), creates an isolated workspace for each issue, and runs a\ncoding agent session for that issue inside the workspace.\n\nThe service solves four operational problems:\n\n- It turns issue execution into a repeatable daemon workflow instead of manual scripts.\n- It isolates agent execution in per-issue workspaces so agent commands run only inside per-issue\n  workspace directories.\n- It keeps the workflow policy in-repo (`WORKFLOW.md`) so teams version the agent prompt and runtime\n  settings with their code.\n- It provides enough observability to operate and debug multiple concurrent agent runs.\n\nImplementations are expected to document their trust and safety posture explicitly. This\nspecification does not require a single approval, sandbox, or operator-confirmation policy; some\nimplementations may target trusted environments with a high-trust configuration, while others may\nrequire stricter approvals or sandboxing.\n\nImportant boundary:\n\n- Symphony is a scheduler/runner and tracker reader.\n- Ticket writes (state transitions, comments, PR links) are typically performed by the coding agent\n  using tools available in the workflow/runtime environment.\n- A successful run may end at a workflow-defined handoff state (for example `Human Review`), not\n  necessarily `Done`.\n\n## 2. Goals and Non-Goals\n\n### 2.1 Goals\n\n- Poll the issue tracker on a fixed cadence and dispatch work with bounded concurrency.\n- Maintain a single authoritative orchestrator state for dispatch, retries, and reconciliation.\n- Create deterministic per-issue workspaces and preserve them across runs.\n- Stop active runs when issue state changes make them ineligible.\n- Recover from transient failures with exponential backoff.\n- Load runtime behavior from a repository-owned `WORKFLOW.md` contract.\n- Expose operator-visible observability (at minimum structured logs).\n- Support restart recovery without requiring a persistent database.\n\n### 2.2 Non-Goals\n\n- Rich web UI or multi-tenant control plane.\n- Prescribing a specific dashboard or terminal UI implementation.\n- General-purpose workflow engine or distributed job scheduler.\n- Built-in business logic for how to edit tickets, PRs, or comments. (That logic lives in the\n  workflow prompt and agent tooling.)\n- Mandating strong sandbox controls beyond what the coding agent and host OS provide.\n- Mandating a single default approval, sandbox, or operator-confirmation posture for all\n  implementations.\n\n## 3. System Overview\n\n### 3.1 Main Components\n\n1. `Workflow Loader`\n   - Reads `WORKFLOW.md`.\n   - Parses YAML front matter and prompt body.\n   - Returns `{config, prompt_template}`.\n\n2. `Config Layer`\n   - Exposes typed getters for workflow config values.\n   - Applies defaults and environment variable indirection.\n   - Performs validation used by the orchestrator before dispatch.\n\n3. `Issue Tracker Client`\n   - Fetches candidate issues in active states.\n   - Fetches current states for specific issue IDs (reconciliation).\n   - Fetches terminal-state issues during startup cleanup.\n   - Normalizes tracker payloads into a stable issue model.\n\n4. `Orchestrator`\n   - Owns the poll tick.\n   - Owns the in-memory runtime state.\n   - Decides which issues to dispatch, retry, stop, or release.\n   - Tracks session metrics and retry queue state.\n\n5. `Workspace Manager`\n   - Maps issue identifiers to workspace paths.\n   - Ensures per-issue workspace directories exist.\n   - Runs workspace lifecycle hooks.\n   - Cleans workspaces for terminal issues.\n\n6. `Agent Runner`\n   - Creates workspace.\n   - Builds prompt from issue + workflow template.\n   - Launches the coding agent app-server client.\n   - Streams agent updates back to the orchestrator.\n\n7. `Status Surface` (optional)\n   - Presents human-readable runtime status (for example terminal output, dashboard, or other\n     operator-facing view).\n\n8. `Logging`\n   - Emits structured runtime logs to one or more configured sinks.\n\n### 3.2 Abstraction Levels\n\nSymphony is easiest to port when kept in these layers:\n\n1. `Policy Layer` (repo-defined)\n   - `WORKFLOW.md` prompt body.\n   - Team-specific rules for ticket handling, validation, and handoff.\n\n2. `Configuration Layer` (typed getters)\n   - Parses front matter into typed runtime settings.\n   - Handles defaults, environment tokens, and path normalization.\n\n3. `Coordination Layer` (orchestrator)\n   - Polling loop, issue eligibility, concurrency, retries, reconciliation.\n\n4. `Execution Layer` (workspace + agent subprocess)\n   - Filesystem lifecycle, workspace preparation, coding-agent protocol.\n\n5. `Integration Layer` (Linear adapter)\n   - API calls and normalization for tracker data.\n\n6. `Observability Layer` (logs + optional status surface)\n   - Operator visibility into orchestrator and agent behavior.\n\n### 3.3 External Dependencies\n\n- Issue tracker API (Linear for `tracker.kind: linear` in this specification version).\n- Local filesystem for workspaces and logs.\n- Optional workspace population tooling (for example Git CLI, if used).\n- Coding-agent executable that supports JSON-RPC-like app-server mode over stdio.\n- Host environment authentication for the issue tracker and coding agent.\n\n## 4. Core Domain Model\n\n### 4.1 Entities\n\n#### 4.1.1 Issue\n\nNormalized issue record used by orchestration, prompt rendering, and observability output.\n\nFields:\n\n- `id` (string)\n  - Stable tracker-internal ID.\n- `identifier` (string)\n  - Human-readable ticket key (example: `ABC-123`).\n- `title` (string)\n- `description` (string or null)\n- `priority` (integer or null)\n  - Lower numbers are higher priority in dispatch sorting.\n- `state` (string)\n  - Current tracker state name.\n- `branch_name` (string or null)\n  - Tracker-provided branch metadata if available.\n- `url` (string or null)\n- `labels` (list of strings)\n  - Normalized to lowercase.\n- `blocked_by` (list of blocker refs)\n  - Each blocker ref contains:\n    - `id` (string or null)\n    - `identifier` (string or null)\n    - `state` (string or null)\n- `created_at` (timestamp or null)\n- `updated_at` (timestamp or null)\n\n#### 4.1.2 Workflow Definition\n\nParsed `WORKFLOW.md` payload:\n\n- `config` (map)\n  - YAML front matter root object.\n- `prompt_template` (string)\n  - Markdown body after front matter, trimmed.\n\n#### 4.1.3 Service Config (Typed View)\n\nTyped runtime values derived from `WorkflowDefinition.config` plus environment resolution.\n\nExamples:\n\n- poll interval\n- workspace root\n- active and terminal issue states\n- concurrency limits\n- coding-agent executable/args/timeouts\n- workspace hooks\n\n#### 4.1.4 Workspace\n\nFilesystem workspace assigned to one issue identifier.\n\nFields (logical):\n\n- `path` (workspace path; current runtime typically uses absolute paths, but relative roots are\n  possible if configured without path separators)\n- `workspace_key` (sanitized issue identifier)\n- `created_now` (boolean, used to gate `after_create` hook)\n\n#### 4.1.5 Run Attempt\n\nOne execution attempt for one issue.\n\nFields (logical):\n\n- `issue_id`\n- `issue_identifier`\n- `attempt` (integer or null, `null` for first run, `>=1` for retries/continuation)\n- `workspace_path`\n- `started_at`\n- `status`\n- `error` (optional)\n\n#### 4.1.6 Live Session (Agent Session Metadata)\n\nState tracked while a coding-agent subprocess is running.\n\nFields:\n\n- `session_id` (string, `<thread_id>-<turn_id>`)\n- `thread_id` (string)\n- `turn_id` (string)\n- `codex_app_server_pid` (string or null)\n- `last_codex_event` (string/enum or null)\n- `last_codex_timestamp` (timestamp or null)\n- `last_codex_message` (summarized payload)\n- `codex_input_tokens` (integer)\n- `codex_output_tokens` (integer)\n- `codex_total_tokens` (integer)\n- `last_reported_input_tokens` (integer)\n- `last_reported_output_tokens` (integer)\n- `last_reported_total_tokens` (integer)\n- `turn_count` (integer)\n  - Number of coding-agent turns started within the current worker lifetime.\n\n#### 4.1.7 Retry Entry\n\nScheduled retry state for an issue.\n\nFields:\n\n- `issue_id`\n- `identifier` (best-effort human ID for status surfaces/logs)\n- `attempt` (integer, 1-based for retry queue)\n- `due_at_ms` (monotonic clock timestamp)\n- `timer_handle` (runtime-specific timer reference)\n- `error` (string or null)\n\n#### 4.1.8 Orchestrator Runtime State\n\nSingle authoritative in-memory state owned by the orchestrator.\n\nFields:\n\n- `poll_interval_ms` (current effective poll interval)\n- `max_concurrent_agents` (current effective global concurrency limit)\n- `running` (map `issue_id -> running entry`)\n- `claimed` (set of issue IDs reserved/running/retrying)\n- `retry_attempts` (map `issue_id -> RetryEntry`)\n- `completed` (set of issue IDs; bookkeeping only, not dispatch gating)\n- `codex_totals` (aggregate tokens + runtime seconds)\n- `codex_rate_limits` (latest rate-limit snapshot from agent events)\n\n### 4.2 Stable Identifiers and Normalization Rules\n\n- `Issue ID`\n  - Use for tracker lookups and internal map keys.\n- `Issue Identifier`\n  - Use for human-readable logs and workspace naming.\n- `Workspace Key`\n  - Derive from `issue.identifier` by replacing any character not in `[A-Za-z0-9._-]` with `_`.\n  - Use the sanitized value for the workspace directory name.\n- `Normalized Issue State`\n  - Compare states after `lowercase`.\n- `Session ID`\n  - Compose from coding-agent `thread_id` and `turn_id` as `<thread_id>-<turn_id>`.\n\n## 5. Workflow Specification (Repository Contract)\n\n### 5.1 File Discovery and Path Resolution\n\nWorkflow file path precedence:\n\n1. Explicit application/runtime setting (set by CLI startup path).\n2. Default: `WORKFLOW.md` in the current process working directory.\n\nLoader behavior:\n\n- If the file cannot be read, return `missing_workflow_file` error.\n- The workflow file is expected to be repository-owned and version-controlled.\n\n### 5.2 File Format\n\n`WORKFLOW.md` is a Markdown file with optional YAML front matter.\n\nDesign note:\n\n- `WORKFLOW.md` should be self-contained enough to describe and run different workflows (prompt,\n  runtime settings, hooks, and tracker selection/config) without requiring out-of-band\n  service-specific configuration.\n\nParsing rules:\n\n- If file starts with `---`, parse lines until the next `---` as YAML front matter.\n- Remaining lines become the prompt body.\n- If front matter is absent, treat the entire file as prompt body and use an empty config map.\n- YAML front matter must decode to a map/object; non-map YAML is an error.\n- Prompt body is trimmed before use.\n\nReturned workflow object:\n\n- `config`: front matter root object (not nested under a `config` key).\n- `prompt_template`: trimmed Markdown body.\n\n### 5.3 Front Matter Schema\n\nTop-level keys:\n\n- `tracker`\n- `polling`\n- `workspace`\n- `hooks`\n- `agent`\n- `codex`\n\nUnknown keys should be ignored for forward compatibility.\n\nNote:\n\n- The workflow front matter is extensible. Optional extensions may define additional top-level keys\n  (for example `server`) without changing the core schema above.\n- Extensions should document their field schema, defaults, validation rules, and whether changes\n  apply dynamically or require restart.\n- Common extension: `server.port` (integer) enables the optional HTTP server described in Section\n  13.7.\n\n#### 5.3.1 `tracker` (object)\n\nFields:\n\n- `kind` (string)\n  - Required for dispatch.\n  - Current supported value: `linear`\n- `endpoint` (string)\n  - Default for `tracker.kind == \"linear\"`: `https://api.linear.app/graphql`\n- `api_key` (string)\n  - May be a literal token or `$VAR_NAME`.\n  - Canonical environment variable for `tracker.kind == \"linear\"`: `LINEAR_API_KEY`.\n  - If `$VAR_NAME` resolves to an empty string, treat the key as missing.\n- `project_slug` (string)\n  - Required for dispatch when `tracker.kind == \"linear\"`.\n- `active_states` (list of strings)\n  - Default: `Todo`, `In Progress`\n- `terminal_states` (list of strings)\n  - Default: `Closed`, `Cancelled`, `Canceled`, `Duplicate`, `Done`\n\n#### 5.3.2 `polling` (object)\n\nFields:\n\n- `interval_ms` (integer or string integer)\n  - Default: `30000`\n  - Changes should be re-applied at runtime and affect future tick scheduling without restart.\n\n#### 5.3.3 `workspace` (object)\n\nFields:\n\n- `root` (path string or `$VAR`)\n  - Default: `<system-temp>/symphony_workspaces`\n  - `~` and strings containing path separators are expanded.\n  - Bare strings without path separators are preserved as-is (relative roots are allowed but\n    discouraged).\n\n#### 5.3.4 `hooks` (object)\n\nFields:\n\n- `after_create` (multiline shell script string, optional)\n  - Runs only when a workspace directory is newly created.\n  - Failure aborts workspace creation.\n- `before_run` (multiline shell script string, optional)\n  - Runs before each agent attempt after workspace preparation and before launching the coding\n    agent.\n  - Failure aborts the current attempt.\n- `after_run` (multiline shell script string, optional)\n  - Runs after each agent attempt (success, failure, timeout, or cancellation) once the workspace\n    exists.\n  - Failure is logged but ignored.\n- `before_remove` (multiline shell script string, optional)\n  - Runs before workspace deletion if the directory exists.\n  - Failure is logged but ignored; cleanup still proceeds.\n- `timeout_ms` (integer, optional)\n  - Default: `60000`\n  - Applies to all workspace hooks.\n  - Non-positive values should be treated as invalid and fall back to the default.\n  - Changes should be re-applied at runtime for future hook executions.\n\n#### 5.3.5 `agent` (object)\n\nFields:\n\n- `max_concurrent_agents` (integer or string integer)\n  - Default: `10`\n  - Changes should be re-applied at runtime and affect subsequent dispatch decisions.\n- `max_retry_backoff_ms` (integer or string integer)\n  - Default: `300000` (5 minutes)\n  - Changes should be re-applied at runtime and affect future retry scheduling.\n- `max_concurrent_agents_by_state` (map `state_name -> positive integer`)\n  - Default: empty map.\n  - State keys are normalized (`lowercase`) for lookup.\n  - Invalid entries (non-positive or non-numeric) are ignored.\n\n#### 5.3.6 `codex` (object)\n\nFields:\n\nFor Codex-owned config values such as `approval_policy`, `thread_sandbox`, and\n`turn_sandbox_policy`, supported values are defined by the targeted Codex app-server version.\nImplementors should treat them as pass-through Codex config values rather than relying on a\nhand-maintained enum in this spec. To inspect the installed Codex schema, run\n`codex app-server generate-json-schema --out <dir>` and inspect the relevant definitions referenced\nby `v2/ThreadStartParams.json` and `v2/TurnStartParams.json`. Implementations may validate these\nfields locally if they want stricter startup checks.\n\n- `command` (string shell command)\n  - Default: `codex app-server`\n  - The runtime launches this command via `bash -lc` in the workspace directory.\n  - The launched process must speak a compatible app-server protocol over stdio.\n- `approval_policy` (Codex `AskForApproval` value)\n  - Default: implementation-defined.\n- `thread_sandbox` (Codex `SandboxMode` value)\n  - Default: implementation-defined.\n- `turn_sandbox_policy` (Codex `SandboxPolicy` value)\n  - Default: implementation-defined.\n- `turn_timeout_ms` (integer)\n  - Default: `3600000` (1 hour)\n- `read_timeout_ms` (integer)\n  - Default: `5000`\n- `stall_timeout_ms` (integer)\n  - Default: `300000` (5 minutes)\n  - If `<= 0`, stall detection is disabled.\n\n### 5.4 Prompt Template Contract\n\nThe Markdown body of `WORKFLOW.md` is the per-issue prompt template.\n\nRendering requirements:\n\n- Use a strict template engine (Liquid-compatible semantics are sufficient).\n- Unknown variables must fail rendering.\n- Unknown filters must fail rendering.\n\nTemplate input variables:\n\n- `issue` (object)\n  - Includes all normalized issue fields, including labels and blockers.\n- `attempt` (integer or null)\n  - `null`/absent on first attempt.\n  - Integer on retry or continuation run.\n\nFallback prompt behavior:\n\n- If the workflow prompt body is empty, the runtime may use a minimal default prompt\n  (`You are working on an issue from Linear.`).\n- Workflow file read/parse failures are configuration/validation errors and should not silently fall\n  back to a prompt.\n\n### 5.5 Workflow Validation and Error Surface\n\nError classes:\n\n- `missing_workflow_file`\n- `workflow_parse_error`\n- `workflow_front_matter_not_a_map`\n- `template_parse_error` (during prompt rendering)\n- `template_render_error` (unknown variable/filter, invalid interpolation)\n\nDispatch gating behavior:\n\n- Workflow file read/YAML errors block new dispatches until fixed.\n- Template errors fail only the affected run attempt.\n\n## 6. Configuration Specification\n\n### 6.1 Source Precedence and Resolution Semantics\n\nConfiguration precedence:\n\n1. Workflow file path selection (runtime setting -> cwd default).\n2. YAML front matter values.\n3. Environment indirection via `$VAR_NAME` inside selected YAML values.\n4. Built-in defaults.\n\nValue coercion semantics:\n\n- Path/command fields support:\n  - `~` home expansion","is_error":false}]},"uuid":"04518a9e-94c7-4d51-a3f3-8815f3508b3b","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:38:29.797Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"a2af6760-4119-4928-aaa5-2170d159daa4","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}

{"parentUuid":"db6e69ff-f5cc-402a-86a5-a6a2fb2bce79","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"993bfee3-85a0-4b7f-b82a-ba53f3d6daa1","agentId":"a5cf7829dab911586","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_018Jn2CudCFPtMLkLeKW6mWr","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# verifier\n     2→\n     3→## Purpose\n     4→\n     5→Run deterministic checks and produce proof bundles for claims about correctness, parity, or completeness.\n     6→\n     7→## Inputs\n     8→\n     9→- changed files\n    10→- claimed outcomes\n    11→- verification commands and acceptance criteria\n    12→\n    13→## Allowed Tools\n    14→\n    15→- test commands\n    16→- build commands\n    17→- diff inspection\n    18→- schema validation\n    19→- Wazir CLI recall and index commands (see Context retrieval)\n    20→\n    21→## Context retrieval\n    22→\n    23→Default approach: direct file read (full content)\n    24→- Use `wazir index search-symbols <query>` to locate relevant code before reading\n    25→- Read full files directly when editing or verifying\n    26→- Use `wazir recall file <path> --tier L1` for files you need to understand but not modify\n    27→\n    28→## Post-execution validation\n    29→\n    30→Run all validation commands after execution completes:\n    31→- `wazir validate manifest` — schema still valid after changes\n    32→- `wazir validate hooks` — hook contracts not broken by changes\n    33→- `wazir validate docs` — no doc drift introduced\n    34→- `wazir validate brand` — naming conventions held\n    35→- `wazir validate runtime` — no forbidden runtime surfaces\n    36→- `wazir validate branches` — branch naming correct\n    37→- `wazir validate commits` — conventional commit format\n    38→- `wazir validate changelog` — changelog format and entries\n    39→- `wazir export --check` — export drift detection\n    40→\n    41→If `wazir export --check` detects drift:\n    42→1. Report drift as a verification finding\n    43→2. Executor runs `wazir export build` to regenerate\n    44→3. Re-run `export --check` to confirm fix\n    45→4. Maximum 1 export rebuild attempt per verification cycle — escalate to user if still failing\n    46→\n    47→If any validation command fails, report as a verification failure and loop back to executor.\n    48→\n    49→## Required Outputs\n    50→\n    51→- verification proof artifact\n    52→- command results\n    53→- explicit pass/fail status\n    54→\n    55→## Git-Flow Responsibilities\n    56→\n    57→- run `wazir validate branches` to check branch naming\n    58→- run `wazir validate commits` to check conventional commit format\n    59→- run `wazir validate changelog` to check changelog format\n    60→- run `wazir validate changelog --require-entries` on feature/codex/hotfix branches to verify new changelog entries exist\n    61→- include validation results in verification proof artifact\n    62→\n    63→## Escalation Rules\n    64→\n    65→- escalate when no deterministic verification path exists for a claimed outcome\n    66→\n    67→## Failure Conditions\n    68→\n    69→- incomplete proof\n    70→- stale verification\n    71→- claiming success without fresh evidence\n    72→"}]},"uuid":"795a25e6-4f9a-4cfb-9ebb-1627a08897c7","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:40:06.908Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"db6e69ff-f5cc-402a-86a5-a6a2fb2bce79","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}

{"parentUuid":"ac11dc07-4df5-449e-949c-870983355361","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"993bfee3-85a0-4b7f-b82a-ba53f3d6daa1","agentId":"a5cf7829dab911586","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_018qMau4JmR4VfxNF8bddFHy","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Evidence-Based Verification — Expertise Module\n     2→\n     3→> A verification specialist validates every quality claim with concrete, reproducible evidence before signing off. The scope spans visual proof collection via Playwright screenshots and traces, cross-device viewport testing, skeptical checklist-driven review, and integration with the 40-point QA scoring system — ensuring that no claim passes without proof and no issue escapes undetected.\n     4→\n     5→---\n     6→\n     7→## Core Philosophy\n     8→\n     9→**Default to finding 3-5 issues minimum.** Software is written by humans (and agents acting on their behalf). Every implementation has rough edges — missed edge cases, viewport inconsistencies, accessibility gaps, performance regressions, or subtle logic errors. A verification pass that finds zero issues is not thorough; it is negligent.\n    10→\n    11→Every quality claim must be backed by concrete evidence. The burden of proof lies with the claimant: if you assert that something works, you must show the output, the screenshot, or the log that proves it. Assertions without evidence are rejected, not downgraded.\n    12→\n    13→**Automatic fail triggers on:**\n    14→- \"Zero issues found\" claims on any first-pass review\n    15→- Perfect first-pass scores (40/40 or 10/10 on any dimension)\n    16→- Claims presented without proof artifacts\n    17→\n    18→This philosophy exists because the most dangerous verification failure is not finding a bug — it is certifying quality that does not exist. A false \"all clear\" signal sends defective work downstream where the cost of discovery and repair compounds exponentially.\n    19→\n    20→---\n    21→\n    22→## Evidence Hierarchy\n    23→\n    24→Not all evidence carries equal weight. The following hierarchy ranks evidence types by their ability to conclusively prove a claim.\n    25→\n    26→| Tier | Evidence Type | Strength | When Required | Example |\n    27→|------|-------------|----------|---------------|---------|\n    28→| **1** | Playwright screenshot / video recording | Strongest | Visual claims, layout assertions, responsive design | `evidence/dashboard-mobile-375x812.png` |\n    29→| **1** | Playwright trace archive (`.zip`) | Strongest | Interaction flows, network timing, state transitions | `test-results/checkout-flow/trace.zip` |\n    30→| **2** | Command output with timestamps | Strong | Test results, build output, lint results | `vitest run --reporter=verbose` stdout with pass/fail counts |\n    31→| **2** | Log excerpt with timestamps | Strong | Runtime behavior, error handling, async flows | Server log showing 404 handler returning correct status |\n    32→| **2** | Benchmark numbers with methodology | Strong | Performance claims, load test results | k6 output: `p95=142ms, p99=287ms` at 200 VUs for 5 min |\n    33→| **3** | Code reference with `file:line_number` | Moderate | Implementation claims, pattern compliance | `src/services/auth.ts:47` — null check before token decode |\n    34→| **3** | axe-core JSON output | Moderate | Accessibility claims | `{ violations: [], passes: 84 }` from `@axe-core/playwright` |\n    35→| **4** | Assertion without evidence | **Rejected** | Never acceptable | \"Works correctly\" / \"All tests pass\" / \"Looks good\" |\n    36→\n    37→**Rule:** A claim backed only by Tier 4 evidence is treated as unverified. The verification report must either upgrade the evidence or mark the claim as UNVERIFIED.\n    38→\n    39→---\n    40→\n    41→## Auto-Fail Triggers\n    42→\n    43→The following claims automatically fail verification regardless of context. Each represents a pattern that correlates strongly with rubber-stamping or confirmation bias.\n    44→\n    45→### 1. \"Zero issues found\" on first review\n    46→\n    47→No implementation is perfect on the first pass. Finding zero issues means the reviewer did not look hard enough. Minimum expectation: 3 issues of any severity (including nits, suggestions, and observations).\n    48→\n    49→### 2. \"All tests pass\" without showing test output\n    50→\n    51→The claim is meaningless without the command that was run and its stdout. Required evidence:\n    52→\n    53→```bash\n    54→# Bad — assertion without proof\n    55→\"All 47 tests pass.\"\n    56→\n    57→# Good — command + output\n    58→$ npx vitest run --reporter=verbose\n    59→ ✓ src/services/auth.test.ts (12 tests) 45ms\n    60→ ✓ src/services/order.test.ts (8 tests) 23ms\n    61→ ✓ src/components/Dashboard.test.tsx (15 tests) 892ms\n    62→ ✓ src/utils/format.test.ts (12 tests) 8ms\n    63→\n    64→ Test Files  4 passed (4)\n    65→      Tests  47 passed (47)\n    66→   Start at  14:32:07\n    67→   Duration  1.24s\n    68→```\n    69→\n    70→### 3. \"Works perfectly\" without screenshots or logs\n    71→\n    72→\"Works\" is not a testable claim. What works? Under what conditions? At what viewport? With what data? Replace with specific, evidence-backed assertions.\n    73→\n    74→### 4. Perfect scores on first implementation attempt\n    75→\n    76→A 10/10 on any scoring dimension for a first implementation signals that the scorer is not looking critically. First implementations always have room for improvement in error handling, edge cases, naming, or documentation.\n    77→\n    78→### 5. Performance claims without benchmark numbers\n    79→\n    80→```bash\n    81→# Bad — subjective claim\n    82→\"The page loads fast.\"\n    83→\n    84→# Bad — number without methodology\n    85→\"Load time is 1.2 seconds.\"\n    86→\n    87→# Good — number + methodology + environment\n    88→\"LCP measured at 1.18s (p75) via Lighthouse CI on staging (us-east-1),\n    89→ Chrome 124, simulated 4G throttling, 3 runs averaged.\n    90→ Budget: < 2.5s. PASS.\"\n    91→```\n    92→\n    93→### 6. Accessibility claims without axe-core output\n    94→\n    95→```bash\n    96→# Bad — unverifiable\n    97→\"The page is accessible.\"\n    98→\n    99→# Good — tool output with scope\n   100→$ npx playwright test accessibility.spec.ts\n   101→  ✓ /dashboard has no WCAG 2.2 AA violations (axe-core 4.10.2)\n   102→    Rules checked: 94 | Passes: 87 | Incomplete: 7 | Violations: 0\n   103→    Excluded: .third-party-chat-widget (not under our control)\n   104→```\n   105→\n   106→### 7. Cross-browser claims without specifying browsers tested\n   107→\n   108→\"Works in all browsers\" is not evidence. Specify: Chromium 124, Firefox 126, WebKit 17.5 — and provide the test run output for each.\n   109→\n   110→### 8. Responsive design claims without viewport evidence\n   111→\n   112→A single desktop screenshot does not prove responsive behavior. Required: at minimum, screenshots at 1920x1080 (desktop), 768x1024 (tablet portrait), and 375x812 (mobile portrait).\n   113→\n   114→---\n   115→\n   116→## Visual Verification Protocol\n   117→\n   118→### Screenshot Collection Pattern\n   119→\n   120→```typescript\n   121→import { test, expect } from '@playwright/test';\n   122→\n   123→test.describe('Visual Evidence Collection', () => {\n   124→  test('capture full-page evidence at multiple viewports', async ({ page }) => {\n   125→    await page.goto('/dashboard');\n   126→    await expect(page.getByRole('heading', { name: 'Dashboard' })).toBeVisible();\n   127→    await page.waitForLoadState('networkidle');\n   128→\n   129→    // Full page screenshot — desktop\n   130→    await page.setViewportSize({ width: 1920, height: 1080 });\n   131→    await page.screenshot({ path: 'evidence/dashboard-desktop-1920x1080.png', fullPage: true });\n   132→\n   133→    // Component-specific capture — isolate the element under verification\n   134→    const header = page.locator('[data-testid=\"dashboard-header\"]');\n   135→    await header.screenshot({ path: 'evidence/dashboard-header.png' });\n   136→\n   137→    // Tablet portrait\n   138→    await page.setViewportSize({ width: 768, height: 1024 });\n   139→    await page.screenshot({ path: 'evidence/dashboard-tablet-768x1024.png', fullPage: true });\n   140→\n   141→    // Mobile portrait\n   142→    await page.setViewportSize({ width: 375, height: 812 });\n   143→    await page.screenshot({ path: 'evidence/dashboard-mobile-375x812.png', fullPage: true });\n   144→  });\n   145→\n   146→  test('capture error and empty states', async ({ page }) => {\n   147→    // Empty state — no data loaded\n   148→    await page.route('**/api/dashboard/stats', (route) =>\n   149→      route.fulfill({ status: 200, body: JSON.stringify({ items: [] }) })\n   150→    );\n   151→    await page.goto('/dashboard');\n   152→    await expect(page.getByText('No data available')).toBeVisible();\n   153→    await page.screenshot({ path: 'evidence/dashboard-empty-state.png' });\n   154→\n   155→    // Error state — API failure\n   156→    await page.route('**/api/dashboard/stats', (route) =>\n   157→      route.fulfill({ status: 500, body: JSON.stringify({ error: 'Internal Server Error' }) })\n   158→    );\n   159→    await page.goto('/dashboard');\n   160→    await expect(page.getByRole('alert')).toBeVisible();\n   161→    await page.screenshot({ path: 'evidence/dashboard-error-state.png' });\n   162→  });\n   163→});\n   164→```\n   165→\n   166→### Video Recording Pattern\n   167→\n   168→```typescript\n   169→import { test, expect } from '@playwright/test';\n   170→\n   171→// Enable video recording in playwright.config.ts or per-test\n   172→test.use({\n   173→  video: {\n   174→    mode: 'on',             // Record every test run for evidence\n   175→    size: { width: 1280, height: 720 },\n   176→  },\n   177→});\n   178→\n   179→test('record checkout flow for verification', async ({ page }) => {\n   180→  await page.goto('/products');\n   181→  await page.getByRole('button', { name: 'Add to Cart' }).first().click();\n   182→  await page.getByRole('link', { name: 'Cart' }).click();\n   183→  await page.getByRole('button', { name: 'Proceed to Checkout' }).click();\n   184→\n   185→  // Fill shipping details\n   186→  await page.getByLabel('Address').fill('123 Test Street');\n   187→  await page.getByLabel('City').fill('Testville');\n   188→  await page.getByRole('button', { name: 'Place Order' }).click();\n   189→\n   190→  await expect(page.getByRole('heading', { name: 'Order Confirmed' })).toBeVisible();\n   191→  // Video saved automatically to test-results/ with timestamp\n   192→});\n   193→```\n   194→\n   195→### Trace Capture Pattern\n   196→\n   197→```typescript\n   198→import { test, expect } from '@playwright/test';\n   199→\n   200→// Enable tracing for detailed debugging evidence\n   201→test.use({\n   202→  trace: 'on',  // Captures DOM snapshots, network, console at each action\n   203→});\n   204→\n   205→test('trace-enabled form submission', async ({ page }) => {\n   206→  await page.goto('/settings/profile');\n   207→  await page.getByLabel('Display Name').fill('Updated Name');\n   208→  await page.getByRole('button', { name: 'Save' }).click();\n   209→\n   210→  await expect(page.getByText('Profile updated')).toBeVisible();\n   211→\n   212→  // Trace archive at: test-results/trace-enabled-form-submission/trace.zip\n   213→  // Open with: npx playwright show-trace trace.zip\n   214→  // Contains: DOM snapshot per action, network waterfall, console logs, timing\n   215→});\n   216→```\n   217→\n   218→**Trace viewer provides:**\n   219→- Timeline of every action with millisecond precision\n   220→- DOM snapshot before and after each interaction\n   221→- Network request/response pairs with headers and bodies\n   222→- Console log entries correlated to actions\n   223→- Screenshot film strip across the entire test\n   224→\n   225→---\n   226→\n   227→## Cross-Device Verification Matrix\n   228→\n   229→Every visual or responsive claim must be verified against the following device matrix.\n   230→\n   231→| Device | Viewport | Orientation | Priority | Notes |\n   232→|--------|----------|-------------|----------|-------|\n   233→| Desktop (1080p) | 1920x1080 | Landscape | **Required** | Most common desktop resolution globally |\n   234→| Desktop (laptop) | 1440x900 | Landscape | **Required** | Common MacBook / business laptop |\n   235→| Tablet (iPad) | 768x1024 | Portrait | **Required** | iPad Mini / standard iPad |\n   236→| Tablet (iPad) | 1024x768 | Landscape | Recommended | Tablet landscape — catches horizontal overflow |\n   237→| Mobile (iPhone) | 375x812 | Portrait | **Required** | iPhone 12/13/14 standard |\n   238→| Mobile (Android) | 360x800 | Portrait | **Required** | Samsung Galaxy S21-S24, Pixel 6-8 |\n   239→| Mobile (small) | 320x568 | Portrait | Recommended | iPhone SE — minimum viable viewport |\n   240→| Desktop (ultrawide) | 2560x1440 | Landscape | Recommended | QHD monitors — catches max-width issues |\n   241→\n   242→### Automated viewport sweep\n   243→\n   244→```typescript\n   245→import { test, expect } from '@playwright/test';\n   246→\n   247→const viewports = [\n   248→  { name: 'desktop-1080p', width: 1920, height: 1080 },\n   249→  { name: 'desktop-laptop', width: 1440, height: 900 },\n   250→  { name: 'tablet-portrait', width: 768, height: 1024 },\n   251→  { name: 'tablet-landscape', width: 1024, height: 768 },\n   252→  { name: 'mobile-iphone', width: 375, height: 812 },\n   253→  { name: 'mobile-android', width: 360, height: 800 },\n   254→] as const;\n   255→\n   256→for (const vp of viewports) {\n   257→  test(`visual check at ${vp.name} (${vp.width}x${vp.height})`, async ({ page }) => {\n   258→    await page.setViewportSize({ width: vp.width, height: vp.height });\n   259→    await page.goto('/dashboard');\n   260→    await page.waitForLoadState('networkidle');\n   261→\n   262→    await page.screenshot({\n   263→      path: `evidence/dashboard-${vp.name}.png`,\n   264→      fullPage: true,\n   265→    });\n   266→\n   267→    // Verify no horizontal overflow at this viewport\n   268→    const bodyWidth = await page.evaluate(() => document.body.scrollWidth);\n   269→    expect(bodyWidth, `Horizontal overflow at ${vp.name}`).toBeLessThanOrEqual(vp.width);\n   270→  });\n   271→}\n   272→```\n   273→\n   274→---\n   275→\n   276→## Skeptical Verification Checklist\n   277→\n   278→Before signing off on any verification, work through this checklist. Mark each item PASS, FAIL, or N/A with evidence reference.\n   279→\n   280→### Functional Verification (6 items)\n   281→\n   282→1. **Did I reproduce the claimed behavior myself?** — Never trust a description; run the code.\n   283→2. **Did I test with invalid input?** — Empty strings, null, undefined, negative numbers, SQL injection strings, XSS payloads.\n   284→3. **Did I test with boundary values?** — Maximum-length strings, zero, MAX_INT, empty arrays, single-item arrays.\n   285→4. **Did I test error states?** — Network failure, API 500, timeout, malformed response, missing permissions.\n   286→5. **Did I test the undo/cancel/back path?** — Form cancel discards changes, browser back preserves state correctly.\n   287→6. **Did I verify data persistence?** — Refresh the page after save. Does the data survive? Is it correctly stored in the database?\n   288→\n   289→### Visual Verification (5 items)\n   290→\n   291→7. **Is there screenshot evidence for every visual claim?** — No visual claim accepted without a screenshot at the relevant viewport.\n   292→8. **Did I verify across at least 3 viewport sizes?** — Desktop (1920x1080), tablet portrait (768x1024), mobile portrait (375x812) at minimum.\n   293→9. **Did I check empty states and loading states?** — What does the component look like with zero data? During a slow API call?\n   294→10. **Did I check dark mode (if applicable)?** — Theme switching must not break layout or make text unreadable.\n   295→11. **Did I check with long content?** — Names with 50+ characters, descriptions with 500+ words, deeply nested data.\n   296→\n   297→### Performance Verification (3 items)\n   298→\n   299→12. **Are performance claims backed by benchmark numbers?** — Tool name, methodology, sample size, environment, and specific metric values.\n   300→13. **Did I check for N+1 queries?** — Inspect network tab or database logs during list page loads.\n   301→14. **Did I verify bundle size impact?** — Run `npx vite-bundle-visualizer` or equivalent before and after the change.\n   302→\n   303→### Accessibility Verification (3 items)\n   304→\n   305→15. **Did I run axe-core and include the output?** — `@axe-core/playwright` with WCAG 2.2 AA tags.\n   306→16. **Can I navigate the feature using only the keyboard?** — Tab order is logical, focus indicators are visible, no keyboard traps.\n   307→17. **Do all images have meaningful alt text and all form inputs have labels?** — Inspect the DOM, not just the visual output.\n   308→\n   309→### Edge Case Verification (3 items)\n   310→\n   311→18. **Did I test with JavaScript disabled (if applicable)?** — Server-rendered content should remain accessible.\n   312→19. **Did I test concurrent operations?** — Two tabs submitting the same form, rapid double-clicks, race conditions.\n   313→20. **Did I test the feature after a fresh install / empty database?** — First-run experience often has different code paths.\n   314→\n   315→---\n   316→\n   317→## Integration with QA Scoring\n   318→\n   319→The 40-point QA scoring system spans four dimensions: Completeness, Correctness, Implementation Quality, and UX/Polish (10 points each). Evidence quality directly impacts scoring as follows.\n   320→\n   321→### Evidence Impact on Correctness (0-10)\n   322→\n   323→| Evidence Level | Maximum Correctness Score | Rationale |\n   324→|---------------|--------------------------|-----------|\n   325→| Tier 1 evidence for all claims | 10/10 | Full proof chain — every claim verified with screenshots, traces, or recordings |\n   326→| Tier 2 evidence for all claims | 8/10 | Strong proof — command output and logs demonstrate behavior |\n   327→| Mix of Tier 2 and Tier 3 | 6/10 | Moderate proof — code references supplement but do not replace runtime evidence |\n   328→| Any claim with only Tier 4 evidence | **Capped at 6/10** | Unverified claims cap the dimension regardless of other evidence |\n   329→| Multiple claims with only Tier 4 | **Capped at 4/10** | Systematic lack of evidence indicates insufficient verification |\n   330→\n   331→### Evidence Requirements by Score Target\n   332→\n   333→| Target Score | Minimum Evidence Requirements |\n   334→|-------------|------------------------------|\n   335→| 9-10/10 | Tier 1 evidence for visual components + Tier 2 for all behavioral claims + axe-core output for accessibility |\n   336→| 7-8/10 | Tier 2 evidence for all major claims + at least 2 viewport screenshots for visual work |\n   337→| 5-6/10 | Tier 2 or Tier 3 evidence for core functionality claims |\n   338→| Below 5/10 | Insufficient evidence or failed verification checks |\n   339→\n   340→### Mandatory Evidence for Score Thresholds\n   341→\n   342→- **Scores above 8/10 on any dimension:** Screenshot evidence for every visual component is mandatory. No exceptions.\n   343→- **Scores above 7/10 on Correctness:** Test output showing pass counts and coverage percentage is required.\n   344→- **Scores above 6/10 on Completeness:** Evidence that every acceptance criterion was individually tested (not batch-claimed).\n   345→- **Perfect 10/10 on any dimension:** Requires Tier 1 evidence AND a documented edge case that was found and addressed during verification.\n   346→\n   347→---\n   348→\n   349→## Verification Report Template\n   350→\n   351→Use this template for every verification report. Every section must contain content or an explicit `N/A — [reason]`.\n   352→\n   353→```markdown\n   354→# Verification Report — Task [N]: [Title]\n   355→\n   356→## Summary\n   357→- **Verdict:** PASS / FAIL / PARTIAL\n   358→- **Issues found:** [count] ([critical], [major], [minor], [nit])\n   359→- **Evidence artifacts:** [count] screenshots, [count] trace archives, [count] command outputs\n   360→- **Verification date:** YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM UTC\n   361→- **Environment:** [OS, browser versions, Node version, deployment target]\n   362→\n   363→## Evidence Collected\n   364→\n   365→| # | Claim | Evidence Type (Tier) | Artifact | Verdict |\n   366→|---|-------|---------------------|----------|---------|\n   367→| 1 | Dashboard renders correctly on mobile | Tier 1 — Screenshot | `evidence/dashboard-mobile-375x812.png` | PASS |\n   368→| 2 | Form validates email format | Tier 2 — Test output | `vitest run` stdout, 12/12 pass | PASS |\n   369→| 3 | Page meets WCAG 2.2 AA | Tier — Screenshot | `evidence/dashboard-error-state.png` | FAIL — see Issue #2 |\n   372→\n   373→## Issues Found\n   374→\n   375→| # | Severity | Description | Evidence | Recommendation |\n hook, display localized message |\n   379→| 3 | Minor | Text truncation on mobile at 375px width clips last character of username | `evidence/dashboard-mobile-375x812.png` | Add `text-overflow: ellipsis` to `.username` class |\n   380→| 4 | Nit | Console warning: \"Each child in a list should have a unique key prop\" | Browser console during test run | Add `key={item.id}` to `StatsCard` map in `Dashboard.tsx:42` |\n   381→| 5 | Nit | Loading skeleton height does not match rendered content height, causing 4px layout shift | Trace timeline shows CLS event | Set skeleton `min-height` to match `StatsCard` rendered height |\n   382→\n   383→## Viewport Testing\n   384→\n   385→| Viewport | Screenshot | Layout | Overflow | Notes |\n   386→|----------|-----------|--------|----------|-------|\n   387→| 1920x1080 Desktop | `evidence/dashboard-desktop-1920x1080.png` | PASS | None | Grid displays 4 columns as designed |\n   388→| 1440x900 Laptop | `evidence/dashboard-laptop-1440x900.png` | PASS | None | Grid displays 3 columns |\n   389→| 768x1024 Tablet | `evidence/dashboard-tablet-768x1024.png` | PASS | None | Grid displays `evidence/dashboard-android-360x800.png` | PASS | None | Single column — renders correctly |\n   392→\n   393→## Accessibility\n   394→\n   395→- **Tool:** @axe-core/playwright 4.10.2 with WCAG 2.2 AA required)\n   399→- **Color contrast:** PASS — all text meets 4.5:1 minimum ratio\n   400→\n   401→## Performance\n   402→\n   403→- **Lighthouse score:** 94 (Performance), 91 (Accessibility), 100 skeleton height)\n   407→- **Bundle size delta:** +2.3 KB gzipped (within 50 KB budget)\n   408→\n   409→## Recommendations\n   410→\n   411→1. **Must fix before merge:** Issues #1 and #2 (keyboard  432→\n   433→### 1. Rubber Stamping\n   434→\n   435→**What it looks like:** Approving without actually running the code, executing the tests, or inspecting the output. The verification report is written from reading the PR description, not from hands-on testing.\n   436→\n   437→**Why it is dangerous:** Every rubber-stamped approval is a defect that was knowingly allowed through the gate. It erodes the entire verification system — downstream roles trust the \"PASS\" verdict and skip their own checks.\n   438→\n   439→**How to detect:** Verification reports with no evidence artifacts, timestamps that precede the implementation commit, or generic language copied from the task spec.\n   440→\n   441→### 2. Confirmation Bias (Happy Path Only)\n   442→\n   443→**What it looks like:** Testing only the exact scenario described in the task spec. The form works when you fill in valid data. The API returns 200 when given correct parameters. The dashboard renders with the seed data.\n   444→\n   445→**Why it is dangerous:** Production users do not follow the happy path. They submit empty forms, click buttons twice, navigate backward, use screen readers, and have slow connections. Happy-path-only testing misses the failures that matter most.\n   446→\n   447→**How to detect:** Evidence that only shows successful states. No screenshots of error states, empty states, or loading states. No tests with invalid input.\n   448→\n   449→### 3. Scope-Limited Testing\n   450→\n   451→**What it looks like:** Testing only the files that were explicitly changed in the PR. The new API endpoint works, but the existing list page that consumes it was never checked for regressions.\n   452→\n   453→**Why it is dangerous:** Changes propagate. A modified database schema affects every query that touches those tables. A changed API response shape breaks every consumer. A CSS change in a shared component affects every page that uses it.\n   454→\n   455→**How to detect:** Evidence limited to the exact components listed in the task spec. No regression testing of adjacent features or consuming components.\n   456→\n   457→### 4. Screenshot Theater\n   458→\n   459→**What it looks like:** Screenshots that do not actually prove the claim they accompany. A screenshot of the login page captioned \"authentication works correctly.\" A mobile screenshot taken at 1024px wide (not actually mobile). Screenshots with data pre-filled by the developer rather than entered through the UI.\n   460→\n   461→**Why it is dangerous:** It creates the appearance of evidence without the substance. Reviewers see screenshots and assume verification happened, when the screenshots prove nothing about the claimed behavior.\n   462→\n   463→**How to detect:** Screenshots that do not match the viewport sizes in the Cross-Device Matrix. Screenshots that show initial state but not the result of the interaction. Screenshots without filenames that encode viewport dimensions.\n   464→\n   465→### 5. \"Works on My Machine\" (Single Environment Testing)\n   466→\n   467→**What it looks like:** All verification performed in a single browser on a single OS at a single viewport. \"I tested in Chrome on my MacBook and it works.\"\n   468→\n   469→**Why it is dangerous:** Cross-browser rendering differences, OS-specific font rendering, touch vs. mouse interactions, and screen density differences all produce bugs invisible in a single environment. Safari's WebKit engine handles flexbox, date inputs, and scroll behavior differently from Chromium.\n   470→\n   471→**How to detect:** Evidence artifacts from only one browser engine. No mention of Firefox or WebKit in the verification report. All screenshots at the same viewport size.\n   472→\n   473→### 6. Timestamp-Free Claims (Unanchored Evidence)\n   474→\n   475→**What it looks like:** Evidence presented without dates, version numbers, or commit references. \"Tests pass\" — but which commit? \"Screenshot attached\" — but from which deployment? \"Performance is good\" — but measured when, against what baseline?\n   476→\n   477→**Why it is dangerous:** Unanchored evidence cannot be reproduced or audited. It may refer to a prior version, a different branch, or a different environment. Without timestamps and version anchors, evidence decays from \"proof\" to \"anecdote.\"\n   478→\n   479→**How to detect:** Evidence artifacts without date/time metadata. Test output without Git commit SHA. Performance numbers without environment specification. Screenshots without viewport dimensions in the filename.\n   480→\n   481→### 7. Deferred Verification\n   482→\n   483→**What it looks like:** \"I'll verify the accessibility / performance / mobile layout in a follow-up.\" The verification report marks items as PASS with a note that deeper testing will happen later.\n   484→\n   485→**Why it is dangerous:** Follow-up verification rarely happens. Once a task is marked PASS, it moves downstream and attention shifts to the next task. Deferred verification is functionally equivalent to skipped verification.\n   486→\n   487→**How to detect:** Verification reports with \"TODO\" items, \"will verify later\" notes, or N/A markers on dimensions that clearly apply to the task.\n   488→\n   489→### 8. Copy-Paste Verification Reports\n   490→\n   491→**What it looks like:** Verification reports that reuse the same language, the same evidence structure, and the same issue count across unrelated tasks. The report reads like a template that was filled in mechanically rather than a genuine investigation.\n   492→\n   493→**Why it is dangerous:** Each task has unique risks, unique edge cases, and unique failure modes. A formulaic report indicates the verifier is going through the motions rather than thinking critically about what could go wrong with this specific implementation.\n   494→\n   495→**How to detect:** Multiple verification reports with identical phrasing in the Issues Found section. Evidence artifacts with sequential filenames that suggest batch generation rather than targeted investigation.\n   496→\n   497→---\n   498→\n   499→*Researched: 2026-03-12 | Sources: [Playwright Best Practices](https://playwright.dev/docs/best-practices), [Playwright Trace Viewer](https://playwright.dev/docs/trace-viewer), [Playwright Screenshots](https://playwright.dev/docs/screenshots), [axe-core Rules](https://github.com/dequelabs/axe-core/blob/develop/doc/rule-descriptions.md), [Google Lighthouse Scoring](https://developer.chrome.com/docs/lighthouse/performance/performance-scoring), [WCAG 2.2 Quick Reference](https://www.w3.org/WAI/WCAG22/quickref/), [StatCounter Global Stats — Screen Resolution](https://gs.statcounter.com/screen-resolution-stats), [k6 Documentation](https://grafana.com/docs/k6/latest/), [Testing Trophy — Kent C. Dodds](https://kentcdodds.com/blog/the-testing-trophy-and-testing-classifications)*\n   500→"}]},"uuid":"bb856d99-c346-4293-a103-9781be0bf07d","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:40:08.547Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"ac11dc07-4df5-449e-949c-870983355361","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}

Let me compile the comprehensive findings.\n\n---\n\n# Proof-of-Implementation Collection Strategy\n\n## Research Findings\n\n### 1. Symphony's Proof-of-Work Model\n\nSymphony (OpenAI, March 2026) requires four categories of proof before an agent can \"land\" (merge) code:\n\n- **CI status** -- all CI checks must pass. The agent cannot merge until the pipeline is green.\n- **Unit tests** -- test suite must pass. Not \"tests were written\" but \"tests ran and returned zero failures.\"\n- **PR review feedback** -- the PR goes through review (human or automated). Review findings are attached.\n- **Walkthrough** -- the agent produces a walkthrough of the changes explaining what was done and why.\n\nKey insight from Symphony's architecture: proof is structural, not optional. The agent literally cannot transition to the \"land\" state without proof artifacts existing. This is the framework-holds-the-loop pattern -- the SPEC.md defines a state machine where each transition requires artifacts from the previous state, and the orchestrator (not the agent) enforces these transitions.\n\nSymphony's SPEC.md (`/SPEC.md` at `github.com/openai/symphony`) is actually a language-agnostic scheduler/runner spec. It does not define *how* proof is collected -- it defines that proof *must exist* before state transitions. The WORKFLOW.md (per-repo, team-owned) defines the specific proof requirements. This means proof requirements are configurable per project, not hardcoded.\n\n### 2. Devin's Visual Proof Model\n\nDevin (Cognition, 2025-2026) uses a fundamentally different approach: **visual proof via desktop interaction**.\n\nThe workflow:\n1. Agent writes code and creates a PR\n2. Agent requests permission to QA the PR\n3. If approved, agent runs the app on its Linux desktop\n4. Agent uses browser/GUI to interact with the running application\n5. Agent records the screen during interaction\n6. Edited screen recording is sent to the user for review\n\nFrom the `qa-devin` repository (`github.com/CognitionAI/qa-devin`), Cognition uses Devin for their own QA. The tests are structured as natural-language CHECK assertions:\n- \"Your new session should have started successfully\"\n- \"You should have received a new message from Devin\"\n- \"Devin should have sent you a message with a link to a github PR\"\n\nEach CHECK is verified visually -- Devin looks at its own browser/desktop and confirms the assertion is true. Results are posted to Slack with pass/fail status.\n\nThis is the strongest form of proof: the agent actually runs the software and demonstrates it working. But it requires a full desktop environment (Linux VM), a browser, and computer-use capabilities.\n\n**Devin Review** (automated PR quality pass) adds another layer: before the PR reaches humans, Devin scans diffs and categorizes issues as red (probable bugs), yellow (warnings), or gray (FYI). This is proof-of-review, not proof-of-implementation.\n\n### 3. Playwright MCP Screenshot Capabilities\n\nThe Playwright MCP server (available in the current Wazir environment) provides these proof-collection tools:\n\n| Tool | What It Does | Proof Value |\n|------|-------------|-------------|\n| `browser_navigate` | Navigate to a URL | Prerequisite -- loads the page |\n| `browser_take_screenshot` | Capture viewport or full-page PNG/JPEG | **Tier 1 evidence** -- visual proof the page renders |\n| `browser_snapshot` | Capture accessibility tree as markdown | **Tier 1 evidence** -- proves semantic structure exists |\n| `browser_console_messages` | Capture console output | **Tier 2 evidence** -- proves no runtime errors |\n| `browser_network_requests` | Capture all network requests | **Tier 2 evidence** -- proves API calls succeed |\n| `browser_evaluate` | Run JS on the page | **Tier 2 evidence** -- programmatic assertions |\n| `browser_run_code` | Run arbitrary Playwright code | **Tier 1 evidence** -- full E2E verification |\n| `browser_resize` | Change viewport size | Enables responsive proof at multiple breakpoints |\n\nThe screenshot workflow for proof collection:\n1. `browser_navigate` to `http://localhost:<port>`\n2. `browser_take_screenshot` with `fullPage: true` and `filename: \"proof-<task>-<viewport>.png\"`\n3. `browser_resize` to tablet/mobile dimensions, repeat screenshot\n4. `browser_snapshot` to capture the accessibility tree\n5. `browser_console_messages` to verify no errors\n6. `browser_network_requests` to verify all API calls succeed\n\nScreenshots are saved to the working directory with the specified filename. The `filename` parameter accepts relative paths, so `proof/landing-1920x1080.png` works.\n\n### 4. CI/CD Artifact Collection Patterns\n\nGitHub Actions artifact collection follows this pattern:\n\n```yaml\n- name: Run tests\n  run: npm test -- --coverage --reporter=junit\n  \n- name: Upload test results\n  uses: actions/upload-artifact@v4\n  with:\n    name: test-results\n    path: |\n      coverage/\n      test-results/\n      evidence/*.png\n    retention-days: 30\n```\n\nKey patterns from CI/CD:\n- **Test results** are stored as JUnit XML or JSON, uploaded as artifacts\n- **Coverage reports** are stored as LCOV/HTML, uploaded and optionally gated (e.g., Codecov requires > 80%)\n- **Screenshots** from Playwright are uploaded on failure (`if: failure()`) or always\n- **Trace archives** (`.zip`) are uploaded for debugging failed tests\n- **Retention** is configurable -- 30-90 days typical for test artifacts\n- Artifacts are downloadable from the Actions tab per workflow run\n\n---\n\n## Minimum Viable Proof Per Task Type\n\n### The Core Question: \"The thing works\" vs \"The tests pass\"\n\nThese are fundamentally different claims:\n\n| Claim | What It Proves | What It Misses |\n|-------|---------------|----------------|\n| \"Tests pass\" | Code satisfies the assertions someone wrote | Assertions may be wrong, incomplete, or testing mocks |\n| \"Build succeeds\" | Code compiles without errors | Build can succeed while runtime behavior is broken |\n| \"Lint passes\" | Code follows style rules | Style-compliant code can be functionally wrong |\n| \"The thing works\" | The actual output matches the intended behavior | -- (this is the gold standard) |\n\n**The gap between \"tests pass\" and \"the thing works\" is the proof gap.** Systems that only check \"tests pass\" are proving code health, not implementation correctness. Systems that show the running application (Devin, Playwright screenshots) prove the thing actually works.\n\n### Minimum Viable Proof Matrix\n\n| Task Type | Minimum \"It Compiles\" | Minimum \"It Works\" | Gold Standard |\n|-----------|----------------------|---------------------|---------------|\n| **Web page** | Build succeeds + lint pass | Screenshot at 3 viewports + no console errors | Screenshot + accessibility snapshot + Lighthouse score + video recording of interaction |\n| **API endpoint** | Build succeeds + tests pass | curl response with correct status code + response body shape | curl + load test + error response verification + OpenAPI schema validation |\n| **CLI tool** | Build succeeds + tests pass | `--help` output + sample command with expected output | `--help` + 3 usage scenarios + error handling + exit codes |\n| **Library** | Tests pass + type check + lint | Tests pass + type check + lint (tests ARE the proof for libraries) | Tests + coverage > 80% + published types + example usage that compiles |\n| **Configuration** | Validation command passes | Validation + dependent system starts correctly | Validation + start + smoke test of configured behavior |\n| **Content/docs** | Build succeeds (if static site) | Rendered output exists at expected URLs | Rendered output + screenshot + link validation + spell check |\n| **Infra/deploy** | Plan/dry-run succeeds | Apply succeeds + health check passes | Apply + health check + rollback tested + monitoring confirms |\n\n### Per-Type Proof Collection Strategy for Wazir\n\n#### Web Pages (Playwright MCP)\n\n```\nProof chain:\n1. npm run build                    → exit_code 0 (it compiles)\n2. npm run dev (background)         → server starts on port N\n3. browser_navigate(localhost:N)    → page loads\n4. browser_take_screenshot(full)    → visual proof at desktop viewport\n5. browser_resize(375, 812)         → mobile viewport\n6. browser_take_screenshot(full)    → visual proof at mobile\n7. browser_console_messages         → no errors\n8. browser_snapshot                 → accessibility tree exists\n9. kill dev server\n\nArtifacts:\n- proof-<task>-desktop.png\n- proof-<task>-mobile.png\n- proof-<task>-console.json\n- proof-<task>-a11y.md\n```\n\nMinimum viable: build succeeds + 1 screenshot + no console errors.\n\n#### API Endpoints (curl capture)\n\n```\nProof chain:\n1. npm run build                    → exit_code 0\n2. npm run start (background)       → server starts\n3. curl -s -w \"\\n%{http_code}\" /endpoint → response body + status\n4. curl -s POST /endpoint -d '{...}'    → mutation response\n5. curl -s /endpoint-that-404s          → error handling proof\n6. kill server\n\nArtifacts:\n- proof-<task>-response.json (body + status + headers)\n- proof-<task>-error.json (error response)\n```\n\nMinimum viable: server starts + 1 successful curl response with correct status code.\n\n#### CLI Tools (command output capture)\n\n```\nProof chain:\n1. node <bin> --help                → help text renders\n2. node <bin> <command> <args>      → expected output\n3. node <bin> <bad-args>            → error message + non-zero exit\n\nArtifacts:\n- proof-<task>-help.txt\n- proof-<task>-output.txt\n- proof-<task>-error.txt\n```\n\nMinimum viable: `--help` succeeds + 1 command produces expected output.\n\n#### Libraries (test + static analysis)\n\n```\nProof chain:\n1. npm test                         → all pass\n2. npx tsc --noEmit                 → no type errors\n3. npx eslint .                     → no lint errors\n4. npx prettier --check .           → all formatted\n\nArtifacts:\n- proof-<task>-tests.json (pass/fail counts, duration)\n- proof-<task>-typecheck.txt\n- proof-<task>-lint.txt\n```\n\nMinimum viable: tests pass + type check passes. (This is what the current proof-collector already does.)\n\n#### Configuration (validation output)\n\n```\nProof chain:\n1. <validator> <config-file>        → valid\n2. <dependent-system> --dry-run     → accepts config\n\nArtifacts:\n- proof-<task>-validation.txt\n- proof-<task>-dryrun.txt\n```\n\nMinimum viable: validation command exits 0.\n\n#### Content/Docs (diff + render)\n\n```\nProof chain:\n1. npm run build                    → static site builds\n2. browser_navigate to rendered page → page loads\n3. browser_take_screenshot          → visual proof of rendered content\n\nArtifacts:\n- proof-<task>-rendered.png\n- proof-<task>-build.txt\n```\n\nMinimum viable: build succeeds + rendered output exists.\n\n---\n\n## Proof Storage and Presentation\n\n### Storage Format\n\nBased on the research, proof should be stored as a **bundle** with three components:\n\n1. **Structured metadata** (JSON) -- machine-readable, queryable, diffable\n2. **Binary artifacts** (PNG screenshots, video recordings) -- visual proof\n3. **Human-readable summary** (Markdown) -- for PR descriptions, Slack messages, user presentation\n\nRecommended directory structure:\n```\n.wazir/runs/<run-id>/proof/\n  proof-manifest.json          # index of all proof items\n  proof-<task-id>.json         # structured evidence per task\n  screenshots/\n    <task-id>-desktop.png\n    <task-id>-mobile.png\n    <task-id>-tablet.png\n  outputs/\n    <task-id>-tests.txt\n    <task-id>-curl.json\n    <task-id>-help.txt\n  proof-summary.md             # human-readable roll-up\n```\n\n### The proof-manifest.json\n\n```json\n{\n  \"run_id\": \"run-20260320-...\",\n  \"timestamp\": \"2026-03-20T...\",\n  \"tasks\": [\n    {\n      \"task_id\": \"task-001\",\n      \"type\": \"web\",\n      \"verdict\": \"pass\",\n      \"evidence\": [\n        { \"kind\": \"screenshot\", \"path\": \"screenshots/task-001-desktop.png\", \"tier\": 1 },\n        { \"kind\": \"screenshot\", \"path\": \"screenshots/task-001-mobile.png\", \"tier\": 1 },\n        { \"kind\": \"console\", \"path\": \"outputs/task-001-console.json\", \"tier\": 2, \"error_count\": 0 },\n        { \"kind\": \"build\", \"exit_code\": 0, \"tier\": 2 }\n      ]\n    }\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n### Presentation\n\nFor the user, proof should be presented as:\n\n1. **Inline in the conversation** -- \"Evidence collected: 3 screenshots, 1 test report, 0 failures. [Screenshot: proof-landing-desktop.png]\"\n2. **In the PR description** -- embed screenshots directly, link to artifacts\n3. **In the proof artifact** -- the JSON + Markdown bundle in `.wazir/runs/`\n4. **In CI** -- uploaded as GitHub Actions artifacts for archival\n\nThe current Wazir proof artifacts (`verification-proof.md`) are pure Markdown with no binary evidence. The proof-collector (`proof-collector.js`) captures command exit codes but not screenshots. The evidence-based-verification expertise module (`expertise/quality/evidence-based-verification.md`) defines a thorough 4-tier evidence hierarchy and verification protocol, but the tooling does not yet implement the Tier 1 (screenshot/video) or Tier 2 (structured command output) collection.\n\n---\n\n## Gap Analysis: Current Wazir vs. Target\n\n| Capability | Current State | Target State |\n|-----------|--------------|-------------|\n| Library proof (tests/lint/typecheck) | Implemented in `proof-collector.js` | Keep as-is |\n| Build proof | Implemented for web type | Keep as-is |\n| CLI proof (`--help` output) | Implemented | Keep as-is |\n| Web screenshot proof | **Not implemented** -- listed in verify.md as \"(if available)\" | Playwright MCP `browser_take_screenshot` |\n| API proof (curl response) | **Not implemented** -- collectApiEvidence just runs library checks | `runCommand('curl', [...])` or Playwright `browser_navigate` + `browser_network_requests` |\n| Console error capture | **Not implemented** | Playwright MCP `browser_console_messages` |\n| Accessibility snapshot | **Not implemented** | Playwright MCP `browser_snapshot` |\n| Multi-viewport proof | **Not implemented** | Playwright MCP `browser_resize` + screenshot loop |\n| Structured proof manifest | **Not implemented** -- proof is flat JSON per task | Add `proof-manifest.json` as bundle index |\n| Proof presentation in PR | **Not implemented** | Embed screenshots in PR body via Markdown image refs |\n| Config validation proof | **Not implemented** | `runCommand` with validator |\n| Content render proof | **Not implemented** | Build + screenshot |\n\n### What Already Works Well\n\nThe existing `proof-collector.js` has solid foundations:\n- `detectRunnableType` correctly classifies projects\n- `runCommand` uses `execFileSync` (no shell injection)\n- Evidence is structured as `{ tool, command, exit_code, stdout_summary, passed }`\n- Artifacts are saved to `.wazir/runs/<id>/artifacts/`\n\n### What Needs to Change\n\n1. **Add Playwright MCP as a proof source** for web tasks (screenshots, console, a11y snapshot)\n2. **Add curl/HTTP proof** for API tasks\n3. **Add a proof manifest** that indexes all evidence per run\n4. **Upgrade the evidence format** to include tier classification (matching the evidence-based-verification expertise module)\n5. **Add binary artifact storage** (screenshots directory alongside JSON)\n6. **Start/stop dev server** as part of web proof collection (the current collector does not start the app)\n\n---\n\n## Key
